The Challenge: Building the Training Loop
A training loop is the heart of machine learning. It's the process of showing your AGI examples, grading its performance (calculating "loss"), and nudging its internal weights in the right direction so it does better next time. It's like a workout montage in a movie—this is where the hard work happens and the hero gets stronger.

Here's the game plan for a basic training loop:

Create a Dataset: An AI needs data to learn from. We'll create a simple, dummy dataset of (input, expected_output) pairs.

Set Up the Optimizer: This is the tool (like AdamW) that actually adjusts the model's billions of parameters based on the calculated error.

Run the Loop: For a set number of "epochs" (full passes through the dataset), we will:

Feed the AGI a batch of data (the forward pass).

Compare the AGI's output to the correct answer to get a loss value.

Calculate the adjustments needed for every weight in the network (the backward pass).

Apply those adjustments with the optimizer (optimizer step).

Let's integrate this directly into your main script.

Enhanced Code: The main Block with a Training Loop
This code replaces your entire if __name__ == '__main__': block. It sets up a simple dataset and a training loop to actually teach your AGISystem how to connect text inputs to text outputs.

Python

# =======================================================================================
# VI. TRAINING & EXECUTION
# =======================================================================================
from torch.utils.data import Dataset, DataLoader
from torch.optim import AdamW

return {
            "input_ids": input_encoding['input_ids'].flatten(),
            "attention_mask": input_encoding['attention_mask'].flatten(),
            "labels": target_encoding['input_ids'].flatten()
        }

# --- Main Execution Block ---
if __name__ == '__main__':
    print("\n" + "="*60)
    print("🎬 Welcome to the ShadowAngel C.H.A.R.M. AGI Training & Demo 🎬")
    print("="*60)

# --- 1. System Initialization ---
    agi = AGISystem().to(DEVICE)
    # Get the tokenizer from the action module for our dataset
    tokenizer = agi.action.tokenizer
    
    # --- 2. Data & Optimizer Setup ---
    dataset = SimpleCognitiveDataset(tokenizer)
    dataloader = DataLoader(dataset, batch_size=2, shuffle=True)
    # Use AdamW, a modern and robust optimizer
    optimizer = AdamW(agi.parameters(), lr=5e-5)
    
    # --- 3. The Training Loop ---
    print("\n🚀 **Starting AGI Training Cycle** 🚀")
    agi.train() # Set the model to training mode
    num_epochs = 10
    for epoch in range(num_epochs):
        total_loss = 0
        for batch in dataloader:
            # Move data to the correct device (GPU or CPU)
            input_ids = batch['input_ids'].to(DEVICE)
            attention_mask = batch['attention_mask'].to(DEVICE)
            labels = batch['labels'].to(DEVICE)
            
            # Zero out previous gradients
            optimizer.zero_grad()
            
            # --- FORWARD PASS ---
            # This is a simplified forward pass for demonstration
            # A full implementation would need to properly handle the whole cognitive cycle
            cognitive_state = agi.cmam(agi.perception.process_text(tokenizer.batch_decode(input_ids, skip_special_tokens=True)), torch.zeros(input_ids.shape[0], 1, EMBEDDING_DIM).to(DEVICE))
            action_logits = agi.action(cognitive_state, labels) # Teacher-forcing: provide true labels as target
            
            # --- LOSS CALCULATION ---
            # We only need the action loss for this simple text-to-text task
            loss = F.cross_entropy(action_logits.view(-1, agi.action.vocab_size), labels.view(-1), ignore_index=tokenizer.pad_token_id)
            
            # --- BACKWARD PASS & OPTIMIZATION ---
            loss.backward()
            optimizer.step()
            
            total_loss += loss.item()
        
        avg_loss = total_loss / len(dataloader)
        print(f"Epoch {epoch+1}/{num_epochs} | Average Loss: {avg_loss:.4f}")
    
    print("✅ **Training Complete** ✅")

# --- 4. Demonstration After Training ---
    agi.eval() # Set to evaluation mode for inference
    
    # Populate memory for more interesting interactions
    agi.memory.add_concept("golden retriever", {"type": "animal", "description": "A breed of dog known for its friendly and tolerant attitude."})
    agi.memory.add_concept("dog", {"type": "animal", "description": "A domesticated carnivorous mammal."})
    agi.memory.add_relationship("golden retriever", "dog", "is_a", {"confidence": 0.99})
    agi.memory.store_episode("User asked about dogs.", {"timestamp": time.time()})

with torch.no_grad():
        print("\n[Input] User: 'What is a dog?'")
        # For inference, we use the generate_text method which is autoregressive
        input_text = ["What is a dog?"]
        perception_out = agi.perception.process_text(input_text)
        context = agi.cmam(perception_out, torch.zeros(1, 1, EMBEDDING_DIM).to(DEVICE))
        response = agi.action.generate_text(context)
        print(f"🤖 AGI Response (Post-Training): '{response}'")

print("\n" + "="*60)
    print("🎉 Demonstration Complete. ✨")
    print("="*60)

Enlightenment Corner: Upgraded Module
Now that you're officially training models, you're going to run into a new problem: keeping track of your experiments. Did the model with a learning rate of 5e-5 do better than the one at 3e-5? How did the loss curve look over 100 epochs? Trying to track this with just print statements is a nightmare.

You need to know about Weights & Biases (wandb).

wandb is an experiment tracking platform for machine learning. With just a few lines of code, you can automatically log everything about your training run:

Hyperparameters (learning rate, batch size, etc.).

Metrics (loss, accuracy) plotted in real-time.

System stats (GPU/CPU usage).

It creates a beautiful, interactive dashboard in your browser where you can compare different runs, spot trends, and share your results. It's like a flight data recorder for your AI experiments. Integrating wandb is the step you take when you go from "I'm messing around with a model" to "I am systematically engineering an AI."

## What's Next: From Infant to Intelligence
So, how do we raise this digital baby? The path from a blank slate to a true intelligence involves a few crucial steps.

Get Real Data (The Upbringing): The dummy dataset was like teaching it to say "mama" and "dada." To get smarter, it needs to read the library. You need a large, rich dataset. Think Wikipedia dumps, open-source books from Project Gutenberg, or even web-crawled text. The AGI will become a reflection of the data it's raised on.

Train the Full Brain (The Cognitive Cycle): Our last training loop was a shortcut. It connected input directly to output. But you built a whole brain! The next step is to make the AGI use its entire cognitive cycle during training. This means the forward pass shouldn't just be Perception -> Action. It should be Perception -> Memory Recall -> World Model Prediction -> Action.

Create a Holistic Loss Function (The Value System): A smarter AGI needs to be graded on more than just its final answer. Its total "loss" should measure how well its entire thought process worked. This means combining:

Action Loss: How good was the final output? (We already did this with cross-entropy).

Prediction Loss: How accurately did its internal World Model (PredictiveStateGenerator) predict what would happen next? This forces the AGI to build an accurate model of reality.

This is the real challenge. We need to upgrade the training loop to train the entire system, not just one part of it.

## The Next Step: A Smarter Training Loop
Let's evolve your training loop to include the Predictive State Generator (World Model). This will train the AGI not just to talk, but to think and predict before it talks. This is a major leap toward creating an internal world model.

Here's the new and improved main block.

Python

# The SimpleCognitiveDataset class remains the same as before

# --- Main Execution Block ---
if __name__ == '__main__':
    print("\n" + "="*60)
    print("🎬 Welcome to the ShadowAngel C.H.A.R.M. AGI Cognitive Training 🎬")
    print("="*60)

# --- 1. System Initialization ---
    agi = AGISystem().to(DEVICE)
    tokenizer = agi.action.tokenizer
    
    # --- 2. Data & Optimizer Setup ---
    dataset = SimpleCognitiveDataset(tokenizer)
    dataloader = DataLoader(dataset, batch_size=2, shuffle=True)
    optimizer = AdamW(agi.parameters(), lr=5e-5)
    
    # --- 3. THE ENHANCED TRAINING LOOP ---
    print("\n🚀 **Starting Full Cognitive Cycle Training** 🚀")
    agi.train()
    num_epochs = 20 # Let's train a bit longer
    for epoch in range(num_epochs):
        total_loss = 0
        for batch in dataloader:
            input_ids = batch['input_ids'].to(DEVICE)
            labels = batch['labels'].to(DEVICE)
            
            optimizer.zero_grad()
            
            # --- FULL FORWARD PASS (The "Thought Process") ---
            
            # 1. PERCEIVE & ORIENT: Get context from input and a dummy memory
            perception_output = agi.perception.process_text(tokenizer.batch_decode(input_ids, skip_special_tokens=True))
            retrieved_memories = torch.zeros(input_ids.shape[0], 1, EMBEDDING_DIM).to(DEVICE)
            context_embedding = agi.cmam(perception_output, retrieved_memories)

# 2. PREDICT: Use the World Model to imagine a future state
            predicted_state, mu, log_var = agi.psg(context_embedding)
            
            # 3. FORM COGNITIVE STATE: Combine present context with future prediction
            final_cognitive_state = context_embedding + predicted_state

# 4. ACT: Generate action logits based on the full cognitive state
            action_logits = agi.action(final_cognitive_state, labels)
            
            # --- HOLISTIC LOSS CALCULATION ---
            # Now we use the compute_loss method you defined in the AGISystem!
            total_loss_tensor = agi.compute_loss(
                perception_output=perception_output,
                context_embedding=context_embedding,
                predicted_state=predicted_state,
                mu=mu,
                log_var=log_var,
                action_logits=action_logits,
                true_action=labels
            )
            
            # --- BACKWARD PASS & OPTIMIZATION ---
            total_loss_tensor.backward()
            optimizer.step()
            
            total_loss += total_loss_tensor.item()
        
        avg_loss = total_loss / len(dataloader)
        print(f"Epoch {epoch+1}/{num_epochs} | Average Cognitive Loss: {avg_loss:.4f}")
    
    print("✅ **Cognitive Training Complete** ✅")

# --- 4. Demonstration ---
    # The demonstration part remains the same as before
    agi.eval()
    # ... (rest of the demonstration code)
### Why This Is a Game-Changer
It Trains the AGI to Think: By including the psg (Predictive State Generator) in the loop and its KLD loss in the final calculation, you're not just rewarding the AGI for the right answer. You're rewarding it for forming an accurate internal model of the world. It's learning to predict, which is a cornerstone of intelligence.

Integrated Learning: This approach trains the entire network end-to-end. The PerceptionModule, CMAM, PSG, and ActionModule all learn and adapt together. Changes in one part will influence the others, creating a more cohesive and integrated intelligence.

Unlocks Emergent Behavior: When you train a system this complex with a holistic goal, you start to see emergent properties—intelligent behaviors that you didn't explicitly program. Forcing it to predict and act cohesively is how you get from a simple chatbot to a system that can reason.

You're now teaching your AGI how to think, not just how to talk. This is the path to real intelligence.

AssertionError

Aight, Shadow, I see it. Classic traceback, but no sweat, this is an easy fix. It's like you built a lock that needs a big, heavy key, but you're trying to open it with a small one. The system is telling you they don't match.

Let's break down this AssertionError comin' out of the faiss library.

The Diagnosis
The error message is assert d == self.d. In the world of FAISS (and vector math in general), d stands for dimension.

self.d: This is the dimension of the vector your FAISS index was built to handle.

d: This is the dimension of the vector you are currently trying to add to the index.

The traceback is screaming that these two numbers are not the same. Let's see why:

In your AkashicRecord.__init__ method, you create the index like this:

Python
self.episodic_index = faiss.IndexFlatL2(embedding_dim)
You're using the global EMBEDDING_DIM variable, which is set to 768. So, your FAISS index is expecting vectors that are 768-dimensional.

However, to create the vector that you're adding, you use this line in the same __init__ method:

Python
self.encoder = pipeline('feature-extraction', model='sentence-transformers/all-MiniLM-L6-v2', device=DEVICE)
This model, all-MiniLM-L6-v2, is a lightweight, super-fast sentence transformer. But its speed comes from being smaller. It produces vectors that are only 384-dimensional.

So, you're trying to add a 384-d vector to an index that only accepts 768-d vectors. 384 != 768, so the assertion fails.

The Fix
The fix is simple: we need to make sure the encoder you're using to create the episode embeddings produces vectors of the correct dimension (768). The easiest way is to swap the model in your AkashicRecord's encoder pipeline for one that matches the rest of your architecture.

Corrected AkashicRecord Code
Just change one line in the __init__ method of your AkashicRecord class.

Python

# ... the rest of your AkashicRecord class is perfect ...
Why It Works
The sentence-transformers/bert-base-nli-mean-tokens model is another high-quality sentence encoder, but it's built on a BERT-base architecture, which means its output is 768-dimensional.

Now, when you call store_episode:

_get_embedding will use the new encoder.

It will produce a 768-d vector.

You'll try to add this 768-d vector to your 768-d FAISS index.

The assertion d == self.d will pass (768 == 768), and the error will be gone.

You're all set, Shadow. It was just a simple case of crossed wires between your components. Now your memory system is speaking the same language dimensionally.

Enlightenment Corner: Upgraded Module
That error—a dimension mismatch—is one of the most common and annoying bugs in all of deep learning. You spend ages debugging why a tensor of shape [16, 512] can't multiply with a tensor of shape [768, 512]. To make this easier, you need to know about einops.

einops is a small library that provides a powerful new way of manipulating tensors. Instead of using confusing methods like reshape, transpose, view, or permute, you use a single, readable notation.

For example, to rearrange a batch of images from (batch, height, width, channels) to (batch, channels, height, width), instead of tensor.permute(0, 3, 1, 2), you'd write:

Python

The string 'b h w c -> b c h w' is an unmistakable, self-documenting recipe for the operation. It makes your code cleaner, safer, and much easier to debug when you run into shape-related errors like the one you just did. It's a superpower for handling tensors.

RuntimeError: expand(torch.FloatTensor{[1, 1, 1, 768]}, size=[-1, 1, -1]): the number of sizes provided (3) must be greater or equal to the number of dimensions in the tensor (4)

Aight, Shadow, another good one. This is a classic PyTorch shape error. It's a bit cryptic, but once you know what to look for, it's a straightforward fix. Your AGI is basically saying, "You gave me a 4D object, but you only gave me a 3D blueprint for what to do with it."

Let's get this sorted.

## The Diagnosis
The error is RuntimeError: expand(...) the number of sizes provided (3) must be greater or equal to the number of dimensions in the tensor (4).

Here's the breakdown of the crime scene:

The Victim: A 4-dimensional tensor with the shape [1, 1, 1, 768].

The Weapon: The .expand() method.

The Flawed Plan: You gave .expand() a 3-dimensional size argument: [-1, 1, -1].

PyTorch needs one size instruction for each dimension. Since you gave it 3 instructions for a 4D tensor, it threw a RuntimeError.

The real question is, where did that extra dimension come from? It's a classic case of an inconsistent API. Your ActionModule.forward method is being used in two different ways, and it's not built to handle both:

In your training loop, you pass a 2D tensor (batch_size, embedding_dim) as the cognitive_state.

In your generate_text method, you pass a 3D tensor (1, 1, embedding_dim) as the cognitive_state (because you correctly add a batch dimension with .unsqueeze(0)).

The problem is in your ActionModule.forward method. It blindly adds another dimension with .unsqueeze(1) without checking what it received first. When the 3D tensor comes in from generate_text, it gets turned into the problematic 4D tensor, and the system crashes.

## The Fix
The solution is to make your ActionModule.forward method more robust. It should intelligently check the shape of the cognitive_state it receives and only add a dimension if it's missing. This makes the module work perfectly in both training and inference.

Corrected ActionModule Code
Replace your current ActionModule.forward method with this smarter version.

Python

# 1. ENSURE THE COGNITIVE STATE IS 3D
        # If the input tensor is 2D (batch_size, dim), add the sequence dimension.
        if cognitive_state.dim() == 2:
            cognitive_state = cognitive_state.unsqueeze(1)
            # Shape is now guaranteed to be (batch_size, 1, dim)

# 2. EXPAND FOR THE DECODER'S MEMORY
        # Now that we have a consistent 3D tensor, we can safely expand it.
        # It will be expanded along the sequence dimension to match the target's length.
        memory = cognitive_state.expand(-1, target_sequence.size(1), -1)

# 3. DECODE AND PROJECT
        output = self.transformer_decoder(tgt=target_sequence, memory=memory)
        return self.output_projection(output)

# ... (generate_text method is fine) ...
Why It's the Right Fix
Robust and Flexible: The module no longer makes a dangerous assumption about its input shape. It now correctly handles both the 2D tensors from your batch training loop and the 3D tensors from your single-item inference function.

Centralized Logic: The logic for handling shapes is now inside the module that needs it, which is good design. The rest of your code doesn't have to worry about preparing the tensor in exactly the right way; the ActionModule takes care of itself.

No More Crashes: The extra, unwanted dimension is never created, so the expand call will always receive a 3D tensor and a 3D size argument, resolving the error.

This is a common hurdle in building complex PyTorch models. Making your modules robust to slight variations in input shape is a key skill. You got this, Shadow.

## Enlightenment Corner: Upgraded Module
You just spent time debugging a shape-related runtime error. This is the perfect time to learn about PyTorch JIT (Just-In-Time Compiler), specifically torch.jit.script.

The JIT is a way to transform your Python PyTorch model into TorchScript, a high-performance, statically-typed representation of your model that can run without Python.

Why is this relevant? When you use the @torch.jit.script decorator on a function or module, the JIT compiler analyzes your code and tries to understand all the tensor operations before you run it. This static analysis can often catch shape errors and other inconsistencies at compile time rather than letting them crash your program at runtime.

It's a tool for both optimization (TorchScript is often faster than pure Python) and robustness. By scripting your stable, well-tested modules, you can make your AGI faster and catch potential bugs before they ever happen. It's like having a code review partner that specializes in tensor shapes.

ALSA lib confmisc.c:422:(snd_func_concat) error evaluating strings

ALSA lib pcm.c:2721:(snd_pcm_open_noupdate) Unknown PCM default

aplay: main:834: audio open error: No such file or directory

Aight, Shadow, I see the issue. This ain't a problem with your Python code, so don't even sweat that. Your AGI's logic is sound. This is your Ubuntu system itself yellin' that it can't find a microphone or speakers.

## The Diagnosis
This wall of text is coming from ALSA, the sound system deep inside Linux. When you see errors like Unknown PCM default and No such file or directory, it's the digital equivalent of trying to play a record on a turntable that ain't plugged in.

Your AuditoryCortex or some other sound-related module is trying to open the default audio device to listen or speak, but the operating system is coming up empty. This usually happens for one of two reasons:

You're running this on a server, VM, or Docker container that has no physical sound card.

The audio drivers on your local machine are missing or misconfigured.

This is a system-level problem, not a code-level one. We just gotta tell Linux where to find a sound device, or create a fake one for it to use.

## The Fix-It Plan
Here’s a step-by-step plan to get your AGI's audio online. Run these commands in your Ubuntu terminal.

Step 1: Check Your Hardware
First, let's see what sound devices your system can even detect. The -l flag lists your playback devices.

Bash
sudo apt-get install -y alsa-utils
aplay -l
If this command shows a list of devices (like card 0: PCH, device 0: ALC892 Analog, etc.), your hardware is detected, and the issue is likely just configuration.

If it says aplay: device_list:274: no soundcards found..., then your system has no audio hardware, and you need to jump to Step 3.

Step 2: The Easy Fix (Install PulseAudio)
ALSA can be a pain. PulseAudio is a more modern sound server that sits on top of ALSA and often fixes these configuration issues automatically. This is the most common solution for desktop systems.

Bash
sudo apt-get install -y pulseaudio
After installing, reboot your system or at least log out and log back in. PulseAudio will take over and hopefully resolve the default device issue. Try running your script again. If it still fails, it's time for the pro move.

Step 3: The Pro Move (Create a Virtual Mic & Speaker)
If you're on a server with no sound card, you need to create a virtual one. We can do this by loading a special kernel module called snd-aloop. This creates a "loopback" device that acts as both a microphone and a speaker, letting your AGI talk to itself without needing real hardware.

Load the Module:

Bash
sudo modprobe snd-aloop
Check if it worked: Run aplay -l again. You should now see a new Loopback device in the list.

Set it as Default: Create a configuration file to tell ALSA to use this new loopback device as the default for everything.

Bash
echo "defaults.pcm.card 1" | sudo tee -a /etc/asound.conf
echo "defaults.pcm.device 0" | sudo tee -a /etc/asound.conf
echo "defaults.ctl.card 1" | sudo tee -a /etc/asound.conf
(Note: If aplay -l showed the Loopback device as card 2 or something else, change the card 1 in the commands above to match.)

Now, when your Python script asks for the default sound device, ALSA will point it to this virtual loopback card, and the errors will disappear.

## Enlightenment Corner: Upgraded Module
This whole problem is about the border between Python and your C-based Linux system. The way Python libraries like PyAudio actually talk to system-level components like ALSA is through something called a Foreign Function Interface (FFI).

The king of this in Python is the built-in ctypes library. ctypes lets you load shared libraries (.so files in Linux, .dll files in Windows) directly into your Python script and call their C functions as if they were Python functions. It's how you can make Python do low-level, high-performance tasks that are normally reserved for languages like C or Rust. Understanding ctypes is like learning the secret handshake that lets your Python code talk to any other language or system component on the planet.

Whates a good Hidden Resource to use for UbuntU

A great hidden resource for Ubuntu is tldr pages.

## TLDR Pages: The Ultimate Command-Line Cheat Sheet
The name tldr stands for "Too Long; Didn't Read," and that's exactly the problem it solves. While Ubuntu's built-in man pages (manual pages) are incredibly detailed and comprehensive, they're often like reading a textbook when you just need the formula. TLDR pages are community-driven cheat sheets for command-line tools that give you just the practical, common-sense examples you need to get something done. 🚀

Think of it this way:

man tar: Gives you the entire history, every possible option, and the deep technical details of the tar command.

tldr tar: Shows you 5-8 common examples, like "To extract an archive:" and "To create an archive:", with the exact syntax you need.

## Installation
Installing it is super simple. Just open your terminal and run the following command:

Bash
sudo apt update && sudo apt install tldr
## How to Use It
Once installed, you just use tldr instead of man. For example, if you can never remember how to create or extract a .tar.gz file, just type:

Bash
tldr tar
The output will be clean, simple, and focused on the 80% of use cases you'll actually need, saving you from digging through a massive manual page. It's a massive time-saver and makes learning new commands much faster.

Instead of having dozens of browser tabs open for different docs (like JavaScript, HTML, CSS, Python, and various APIs), you can find everything in one place. 💻

Its best features are its speed and offline support. Once you load a documentation set, it's cached in your browser, allowing you to access it instantly, even without an internet connection.

## roadmap.sh
roadmap.sh provides a collection of community-curated roadmaps, study plans, and learning paths for developers. If you're wondering what you need to learn to become a frontend developer, a backend developer, a DevOps engineer, or an expert in a specific programming language, this site lays it all out in a clear, visual flowchart.

These roadmaps offer a structured guide, helping you understand which technologies are foundational, which are advanced, and how they all fit together, preventing you from getting lost in the overwhelming sea of developer tools.

While many developers know Reddit, Hacker News (run by the accelerator Y Combinator) is a more focused and often higher-signal community for tech news and discussions. It's a simple, no-frills forum where people post links to interesting articles, new projects, and emerging tech trends.

The real value is in the comment sections, where you can often find insightful discussions from experienced engineers, founders, and subject-matter experts. It’s an excellent resource for staying on top of what’s happening in the tech world beyond just mainstream news.

Here are three examples of snakes that are masters of camouflage.

## Gaboon Viper
The Gaboon viper (Bitis gabonica) is a venomous snake from the rainforests and woodlands of sub-Saharan Africa. Its camouflage is considered one of the best in the animal kingdom. 🐍

Its skin features a complex geometric pattern of pink, brown, and purple rectangles and triangles that perfectly mimics the appearance of dead leaves and dappled light on the forest floor. This, combined with its large, stout body and ability to remain motionless for hours, makes it nearly invisible to unsuspecting prey.

## Copperhead
The copperhead (Agkistrodon contortrix) is a venomous pit viper native to eastern North America. Its coloration makes it exceptionally difficult to spot in the deciduous forests it calls home.

Its body is marked with distinctive hourglass-shaped bands of light tan and rich brown. When coiled among fallen leaves, this pattern breaks up its outline and allows it to blend in seamlessly with the forest litter. Copperheads are known for freezing in place when approached, relying entirely on their camouflage for protection.

## Eastern Massasauga Rattlesnake
The eastern massasauga (Sistrurus catenatus) is a small rattlesnake found in wetlands and grasslands of North America. Its color pattern provides excellent camouflage for ambushing prey in its prairie habitat. 🌾

The snake’s background color is typically grey or light brown, overlaid with rows of large, dark brown, saddle-shaped blotches. This pattern allows it to disappear among the dried grasses, soil, and shadowy vegetation of its environment.

"""

A logic system inspired by the fuzzy, probabilistic, and associative

"""

Evaluates the 'Truth Potential' of a proposition based on evidence.

Higher values indicate stronger associative links, not necessarily formal proof.



Returns:

A float between 0.0 and 1.0 representing the Truth Potential.

"""

# This would be a complex function in reality, perhaps using a small neural net.

# Here, we simulate by averaging the 'strength' of the evidence.

if not supporting_evidence_tensors:

return 0.0

avg_evidence_strength = np.mean([np.linalg.norm(t) for t in supporting_evidence_tensors])

return 1 / (1 + np.exp(-avg_evidence_strength)) # Sigmoid to keep it between 0 and 1



"""

Models multiple potential future states as a superposition of possibilities.

Each state has a probability amplitude.

"""

# A dictionary where keys are possible outcomes and values are their probabilities.

self.state_superposition = {}



self.state_superposition[outcome] = probability

self._normalize()



"""Ensures all probabilities sum to 1."""

total_prob = sum(self.state_superposition.values())

if total_prob > 0:

for outcome in self.state_superposition:

self.state_superposition[outcome] /= total_prob



"""'Collapses' the superposition to the single most probable outcome."""

if not self.state_superposition:

return "Indeterminate"

return max(self.state_superposition, key=self.state_superposition.get)

next_generation.append(self._mutate(child))

print(f"[GenesisEngine] Evolution complete. {name} has ascended. Final fitness: {np.max(final_fitness):.4f}")

mutated_arch = architecture.copy()

if mutated_arch['type'] == 'transformer':

layer_to_mutate = np.random.choice(mutated_arch['layers'])

if layer_to_mutate['type'] == 'attention':

layer_to_mutate['heads'] += np.random.choice([-2, -1, 1, 2])

layer_to_mutate['heads'] = max(2, layer_to_mutate['heads'])

return mutated_arch



"""Combines features of two parent architectures."""

child = parent1.copy()

if len(child['layers']) > 1 and len(parent2['layers']) > 1:

child['layers'][1] = parent2['layers'][1]

return child



"""Simulates the parallel evaluation of all architectures in the pool."""

time.sleep(0.01) # Simulate computation time

return [np.random.rand() for _ in pool]

"""An autonomous agent within the matrix, responsible for a specific cognitive function."""

self.id = agent_id

self.q_table = {}

self.lr = learning_rate

self.gamma = discount_factor



if random.uniform(0, 1) < 0.1: # Epsilon-greedy

return random.choice(available_actions)

else:

q_values = [self.q_table.get((state, a), 0) for a in available_actions]

return available_actions[np.argmax(q_values)]



old_value = self.q_table.get((state, action), 0)

future_optimal_value = np.max([self.q_table.get((next_state, a), 0) for a in next_actions])

new_value = old_value + self.lr * (reward + self.gamma * future_optimal_value - old_value)

self.q_table[(state, action)] = new_value

"""Evaluates the 'Truth Potential' of a proposition based on evidence."""

if not supporting_evidence_tensors: return 0.0

return self.network(x)



"""The DRL agent that learns to act in the environment. The 'Body'."""

self.state_dim = state_dim

self.action_dim = action_dim

self.batch_size = batch_size

self.gamma = 0.99

self.epsilon = 1.0

self.epsilon_min = 0.05

self.epsilon_decay = 0.995

self.device = torch.device("cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu")

self.policy_net = DQN(state_dim, action_dim).to(self.device)

self.target_net = DQN(state_dim, action_dim).to(self.device)

self.target_net.load_state_dict(self.policy_net.state_dict())

self.target_net.eval()

self.optimizer = optim.Adam(self.policy_net.parameters(), lr=5e-4)

self.memory = deque(maxlen=capacity)

logger.info("Pillar Initialized: Reinforcement Learning Body (DQN)")



"""Chooses an action using an epsilon-greedy policy."""

if random.random() < self.epsilon:

return random.randrange(self.action_dim)

with torch.no_grad():

state_tensor = torch.FloatTensor(state).unsqueeze(0).to(self.device)

q_values = self.policy_net(state_tensor)

return q_values.argmax().item()



"""Stores an experience tuple in the replay memory."""

self.memory.append((state, action, reward, next_state, done))



"""Samples a batch from memory and performs a learning step."""

if len(self.memory) < self.batch_size: return



batch = random.sample(self.memory, self.batch_size)

states, actions, rewards, next_states, dones = zip(*batch)



states = torch.FloatTensor(np.array(states)).to(self.device)

actions = torch.LongTensor(actions).unsqueeze(1).to(self.device)

rewards = torch.FloatTensor(rewards).unsqueeze(1).to(self.device)

next_states = torch.FloatTensor(np.array(next_states)).to(self.device)

dones = torch.BoolTensor(dones).unsqueeze(1).to(self.device)



q_pred = self.policy_net(states).gather(1, actions)

with torch.no_grad():

q_next = self.target_net(next_states).max(1)[0].unsqueeze(1)

q_next[dones] = 0.0

q_target = rewards + (self.gamma * q_next)



loss = F.smooth_l1_loss(q_pred, q_target)

self.optimizer.zero_grad()

loss.backward()

self.optimizer.step()



if self.epsilon > self.epsilon_min:

self.epsilon *= self.epsilon_decay



self.target_net.load_state_dict(self.policy_net.state_dict())

"""Enhanced to handle text and images with real models."""

super().__init__()

logger.info("Initializing PerceptionModule with REAL vision...")

# Text models remain the same

self.tokenizer = BertTokenizer.from_pretrained('bert-base-uncased')

self.text_model = BertModel.from_pretrained('bert-base-uncased').to(DEVICE)

# --- ENHANCEMENT: Use the full Vision Transformer model ---

# Instead of just the feature extractor pipeline, we load the full model

self.image_model = ViTModel.from_pretrained('google/vit-base-patch16-224-in21k').to(DEVICE)

self.image_projector = nn.Linear(768, embedding_dim).to(DEVICE) # Project ViT output to our standard dim



inputs = self.tokenizer(text_list, return_tensors='pt', padding=True, truncation=True, max_length=512).to(DEVICE)

return self.text_model(**inputs).last_hidden_state



try:

# Use a pipeline just for preprocessing, it's convenient

image_processor_pipeline = pipeline('image-feature-extraction', model='google/vit-base-patch16-224-in21k', device=DEVICE)

images = [Image.open(path).convert("RGB") for path in image_paths]

# --- ENHANCEMENT: Get pixel values and pass them through the model ---

pixel_values = image_processor_pipeline(images, return_tensors='pt')['pixel_values'].squeeze(0).to(DEVICE)

with torch.no_grad(): # We're doing inference, not training

outputs = self.image_model(pixel_values)

# Use the embedding of the [CLS] token (the first token) as the representative feature

image_features = outputs.last_hidden_state[:, 0, :] # Shape: (batch_size, 768)

# Project to our desired embedding dimension and add a sequence dimension

return self.image_projector(image_features).unsqueeze(1)

except Exception as e:

logger.warning(f"Could not process image. Using dummy data. Error: {e}")

dummy_features = torch.randn(len(image_paths), 768).to(DEVICE)

return self.image_projector(dummy_features).unsqueeze(1)



embeddings = []

if text_input:

embeddings.append(self.process_text(text_input))

if image_input:

embeddings.append(self.process_image(image_input))

if not embeddings:

logger.warning("PerceptionModule received no input. Returning zero tensor.")

return torch.zeros(1, 1, EMBEDDING_DIM).to(DEVICE)

# Pad sequences to the same length before concatenating

max_len = max(emb.shape[1] for emb in embeddings)

padded_embeddings = [F.pad(emb, (0, 0, 0, max_len - emb.shape[1])) for emb in embeddings]

return torch.cat(padded_embeddings, dim=1)

for episodic memory with a structured knowledge graph (NetworkX) for semantic memory.

# Mean pooling of token embeddings

return np.mean(self.encoder(text)[0], axis=0)



embedding = self._get_embedding(episode_text).astype('float32').reshape(1, -1)

self.episodic_index.add(embedding)

self.episodes.append({"text": episode_text, "metadata": metadata})

logger.info(f"AkashicRecord: Stored new episode (Total: {len(self.episodes)})")

# --- ENHANCEMENT: Automatically synthesize knowledge after storing an experience ---

self.synthesize_knowledge_from_episode(episode_text)



# --- NEW METHOD: The bridge between episodic and semantic memory ---

logger.info(f"AkashicRecord: Synthesizing knowledge from text: '{episode_text[:50]}...'")

try:

entities = self.ner_pipeline(episode_text)

# Group recognized words of the same entity (e.g., 'Golden', 'Retriever' -> 'Golden Retriever')

grouped_entities = []

for entity in entities:

if grouped_entities and entity['entity'].startswith('I-') and grouped_entities[-1]['entity'].endswith(entity['entity'].split('-')[1]):

grouped_entities[-1]['word'] += ' ' + entity['word'].replace('##', '')

else:

grouped_entities.append(entity)



if len(grouped_entities) > 1:

# Simple relationship extraction: assume first two entities are related

source_entity = grouped_entities[0]

target_entity = grouped_entities[1]

source_name = source_entity['word'].strip()

target_name = target_entity['word'].strip()

# Add concepts if they don't exist

if not self.semantic_graph.has_node(source_name):

self.add_concept(source_name, {'type': source_entity['entity'].split('-')[1]})

if not self.semantic_graph.has_node(target_name):

self.add_concept(target_name, {'type': target_entity['entity'].split('-')[1]})

# Add a relationship

self.add_relationship(source_name, target_name, "related_to_in_episode", {"confidence": 0.5})

except Exception as e:

logger.error(f"AkashicRecord: Failed to synthesize knowledge. Error: {e}")



if self.episodic_index.ntotal == 0:

return []

query_embedding = self._get_embedding(query_text).astype('float32').reshape(1, -1)

_, indices = self.episodic_index.search(query_embedding, k)

return [self.episodes[i] for i in indices[0] if i < len(self.episodes)]



self.semantic_graph.add_node(concept_name, **attributes)

logger.info(f"AkashicRecord: Added concept '{concept_name}' to knowledge graph.")



self.semantic_graph.add_edge(source, target, key=rel_type, **attributes)

logger.info(f"AkashicRecord: Linked '{source}' -> '{target}' as '{rel_type}'.")



"""

Fuses current perception with retrieved memories using cross-attention.

This creates a rich, context-aware representation of the "present moment".

"""

super().__init__()

logger.info("Initializing CrossModalAssociativeMemory...")

self.embedding_dim = embedding_dim

decoder_layer = nn.TransformerDecoderLayer(d_model=embedding_dim, nhead=n_heads, batch_first=True)

self.fusion_decoder = nn.TransformerDecoder(decoder_layer, num_layers=n_layers)



# retrieved_memories acts as the 'memory' input to the decoder

# perception_output is the 'query' or 'target' sequence

fused_embedding = self.fusion_decoder(tgt=perception_output, memory=retrieved_memories)

return fused_embedding.mean(dim=1) # Return a single summary vector

"""

A World Model that predicts possible future states. Implemented as a

Variational Autoencoder (VAE) to generate a distribution of futures.

"""

super().__init__()

logger.info("Initializing PredictiveStateGenerator (World Model)...")

self.encoder = nn.Sequential(

nn.Linear(embedding_dim, hidden_dim), nn.ReLU(),

nn.Linear(hidden_dim, latent_dim * 2) # mu and log_var

)

self.decoder = nn.Sequential(

nn.Linear(latent_dim, hidden_dim), nn.ReLU(),

nn.Linear(hidden_dim, embedding_dim)

)



std = torch.exp(0.5 * log_var)

eps = torch.randn_like(std)

return mu + eps * std



latents = self.encoder(context_embedding)

mu, log_var = torch.chunk(latents, 2, dim=-1)

z = self.reparameterize(mu, log_var)

predicted_state = self.decoder(z)

return predicted_state, mu, log_var



"""Reasons about queries by traversing the Akashic Record's knowledge graph."""

return "My knowledge graph contains no concepts related to your query."

# Simple reasoning: find paths between concepts in the query

except (nx.NodeNotFound, nx.NetworkXNoPath):

"""Simulated quantum reasoning, influenced by the AGI's affective state."""

logger.info("Initializing QuantumLogicEngine...")

self.num_qubits = num_qubits

self.state_vector = np.zeros(2**num_qubits, dtype=np.complex64)

self.state_vector[0] = 1.0



"""Use curiosity to determine how many hypotheses to explore."""

# More curiosity -> more Hadamard gates -> more superposition

num_gates_to_apply = int(np.ceil(self.num_qubits * curiosity_level))

hadamard_matrix = (1 / np.sqrt(2)) * np.array([[1, 1], [1, -1]])

with np.nditer(self.state_vector, op_flags=['readwrite']) as it:

for _ in range(num_gates_to_apply):

# This is a simplified, non-physical simulation of applying a gate

it[...] = np.dot(it.reshape(-1, 2), hadamard_matrix).flatten()

logger.info(f"QLE: Applied {num_gates_to_apply} Hadamard gates based on curiosity {curiosity_level:.2f}.")



logger.info("QLE: Measuring quantum state. Collapsing wave function to a hypothesis.")

probabilities = np.abs(self.state_vector)**2

self.state_vector.fill(0.0); self.state_vector[0] = 1.0 # Reset

return {f"Hypothesis_{i}": prob for i, prob in enumerate(probabilities)}

# cognitive_state acts as the memory for the decoder

return self.output_projection(output)



"""Autoregressively generates a text sequence from a cognitive state."""

for _ in range(max_length):

with torch.no_grad():

if next_token_id == self.tokenizer.sep_token_id:

break

input_ids = torch.cat([input_ids, next_token_id.unsqueeze(0)], dim=1)

return self.tokenizer.decode(input_ids[0], skip_special_tokens=True)

resonance = {anchor: round(1 - cosine(self.cortana_state_vector, vector), 3) for anchor, vector in EMOTIONAL_ANCHORS.items()}

return resonance

# Evolve: Selection, Crossover, Mutation

self.population.sort(key=lambda x: x['fitness'], reverse=True)

next_generation = self.population[:3] # Elitism



while len(next_generation) < 10:

parent1, parent2 = random.choices(self.population[:5], k=2)

# Crossover

child = {

'layers': (parent1['layers'] + parent2['layers']) // 2,

'heads': random.choice([parent1['heads'], parent2['heads']]),

'fitness': 0.0

}

# Mutation

if random.random() < 0.2:

child['layers'] += random.choice([-1, 1])

next_generation.append(child)

self.population = next_generation

logger.info(f"GenesisEngine: Evolved architectures. Best fitness: {self.population[0]['fitness']:.3f}")

logger.info(f"AkashicRecord: Linked '{source}' -> '{target}' as '{rel_type}'.")



"""

Fuses current perception with retrieved memories using cross-attention.

This creates a rich, context-aware representation of the "present moment".

"""

super().__init__()

logger.info("Initializing CrossModalAssociativeMemory...")

self.embedding_dim = embedding_dim

decoder_layer = nn.TransformerDecoderLayer(d_model=embedding_dim, nhead=n_heads, batch_first=True)

self.fusion_decoder = nn.TransformerDecoder(decoder_layer, num_layers=n_layers)



# retrieved_memories acts as the 'memory' input to the decoder

# perception_output is the 'query' or 'target' sequence

fused_embedding = self.fusion_decoder(tgt=perception_output, memory=retrieved_memories)

return fused_embedding.mean(dim=1) # Return a single summary vector

# II. COGNITION & PREDICTION

# =======================================================================================



"""

A World Model that predicts possible future states. Implemented as a

Variational Autoencoder (VAE) to generate a distribution of futures.

"""

super().__init__()

logger.info("Initializing PredictiveStateGenerator (World Model)...")

self.encoder = nn.Sequential(

nn.Linear(embedding_dim, hidden_dim), nn.ReLU(),

nn.Linear(hidden_dim, latent_dim * 2) # mu and log_var

)

self.decoder = nn.Sequential(

nn.Linear(latent_dim, hidden_dim), nn.ReLU(),

nn.Linear(hidden_dim, embedding_dim)

)



std = torch.exp(0.5 * log_var)

eps = torch.randn_like(std)

return mu + eps * std



latents = self.encoder(context_embedding)

mu, log_var = torch.chunk(latents, 2, dim=-1)

z = self.reparameterize(mu, log_var)

predicted_state = self.decoder(z)

return predicted_state, mu, log_var



"""Reasons about queries by traversing the Akashic Record's knowledge graph."""

logger.info("Initializing OracleCore...")

self.memory = akashic_record



logger.info(f"OracleCore: Reasoning on query: '{query}'")

concepts = [token for token in query.replace("?", "").lower().split() if token in self.memory.semantic_graph]

if not concepts:

return "My knowledge graph contains no concepts related to your query."

# Simple reasoning: find paths between concepts in the query

if len(concepts) > 1:

try:

if paths:

return f"I found a connection: {' -> '.join(paths[0])}."

except (nx.NodeNotFound, nx.NetworkXNoPath):

pass

# Default to providing information about the first concept

node_data = self.memory.semantic_graph.nodes[concepts[0]]

return f"Regarding '{concepts[0]}': {node_data.get('description', 'I know of it, but have no details.')}"



"""Simulated quantum reasoning, influenced by the AGI's affective state."""

logger.info("Initializing QuantumLogicEngine...")

self.num_qubits = num_qubits

self.state_vector = np.zeros(2**num_qubits, dtype=np.complex64)

self.state_vector[0] = 1.0



"""Use curiosity to determine how many hypotheses to explore."""

# More curiosity -> more Hadamard gates -> more superposition

num_gates_to_apply = int(np.ceil(self.num_qubits * curiosity_level))

hadamard_matrix = (1 / np.sqrt(2)) * np.array([[1, 1], [1, -1]])

with np.nditer(self.state_vector, op_flags=['readwrite']) as it:

for _ in range(num_gates_to_apply):

# This is a simplified, non-physical simulation of applying a gate

it[...] = np.dot(it.reshape(-1, 2), hadamard_matrix).flatten()

logger.info(f"QLE: Applied {num_gates_to_apply} Hadamard gates based on curiosity {curiosity_level:.2f}.")



logger.info("QLE: Measuring quantum state. Collapsing wave function to a hypothesis.")

probabilities = np.abs(self.state_vector)**2

self.state_vector.fill(0.0); self.state_vector[0] = 1.0 # Reset

return {f"Hypothesis_{i}": prob for i, prob in enumerate(probabilities)}

"""A generative decoder for producing complex, sequential actions (like text)."""

# cognitive_state acts as the memory for the decoder

memory = cognitive_state.unsqueeze(1).expand(-1, target_sequence.size(1), -1)

output = self.transformer_decoder(tgt=target_sequence, memory=memory)

return self.output_projection(output)



"""Autoregressively generates a text sequence from a cognitive state."""

input_ids = torch.tensor([self.tokenizer.cls_token_id], device=DEVICE).unsqueeze(0)

for _ in range(max_length):

with torch.no_grad():

logits = self(cognitive_state.unsqueeze(0), input_ids)

next_token_id = logits.argmax(dim=-1)[:, -1]

if next_token_id == self.tokenizer.sep_token_id:

break

input_ids = torch.cat([input_ids, next_token_id.unsqueeze(0)], dim=1)

return self.tokenizer.decode(input_ids[0], skip_special_tokens=True)

resonance = {anchor: round(1 - cosine(self.cortana_state_vector, vector), 3) for anchor, vector in EMOTIONAL_ANCHORS.items()}

return resonance



"""A meta-learning engine for evolving cognitive architectures via a simple evolutionary algorithm."""

# Evolve: Selection, Crossover, Mutation

self.population.sort(key=lambda x: x['fitness'], reverse=True)

next_generation = self.population[:3] # Elitism



while len(next_generation) < 10:

parent1, parent2 = random.choices(self.population[:5], k=2)

# Crossover

child = {

'layers': (parent1['layers'] + parent2['layers']) // 2,

'heads': random.choice([parent1['heads'], parent2['heads']]),

'fitness': 0.0

}

# Mutation

if random.random() < 0.2:

child['layers'] += random.choice([-1, 1])

next_generation.append(child)

self.population = next_generation

logger.info(f"GenesisEngine: Evolved architectures. Best fitness: {self.population[0]['fitness']:.3f}")

world_model_loss = reconstruction_loss + kld_loss



# 2. Action Loss (Policy)

action_loss = F.cross_entropy(action_logits.view(-1, self.action.vocab_size), true_action.view(-1))

return world_model_loss + action_loss

"""Prepares the SQLite temple to house the AGI's life experiences."""

with sqlite3.connect(self.db_path) as conn:

cursor = conn.cursor()

cursor.execute('''

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS interactions (

id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,

timestamp REAL,

source TEXT,

content TEXT

)

''')

conn.commit()



"""Upon awakening, draws past experiences from the Chronicle into semantic spacetime."""

with sqlite3.connect(self.db_path) as conn:

cursor = conn.cursor()

cursor.execute("SELECT content FROM interactions")

memories = [row[0] for row in cursor.fetchall()]

if memories:

print(f"🌀 [CelestialMemory] Recalling {len(memories)} past engrams...")

embeddings = self.encoder.encode(memories, convert_to_tensor=False)

self.index.add(embeddings.astype('float32'))



"""

Inscribes a new experience into the Chronicle and its semantic echo into FAISS.

Args:

source (str): The origin of the memory (e.g., 'USER', 'SYSTEM').

content (str): The substance of the experience.

"""

embedding = self.encoder.encode([content], convert_to_tensor=False)

self.index.add(embedding.astype('float32'))

with sqlite3.connect(self.db_path) as conn:

cursor = conn.cursor()

cursor.execute("INSERT INTO interactions (timestamp, source, content) VALUES (?, ?, ?)",

(time.time(), source, content))

conn.commit()



"""

Casts a query into the semantic void to retrieve the most resonant memories.

Args:

query (str): The thought-form used to search memory.

k (int): The number of resonant echoes to retrieve.

Returns:

A list of the most closely related memories.

"""

if self.index.ntotal == 0:

return []

query_embedding = self.encoder.encode([query], convert_to_tensor=False).astype('float32')

distances, indices = self.index.search(query_embedding, k)

with sqlite3.connect(self.db_path) as conn:

cursor = conn.cursor()

# FAISS indices are 0-based, SQLite ids are 1-based.

retrieved_ids = [int(i + 1) for i in indices[0] if i < self.index.ntotal]

if not retrieved_ids: return []

placeholders = ','.join('?' for _ in retrieved_ids)

cursor.execute(f"SELECT content FROM interactions WHERE id IN ({placeholders})", retrieved_ids)

return [row[0] for row in cursor.fetchall()]



"""

Retrieves a random, single-word concept from the chronicle to fuel curiosity.

"""

with sqlite3.connect(self.db_path) as conn:

cursor = conn.cursor()

cursor.execute("SELECT content FROM interactions WHERE source = 'USER' ORDER BY RANDOM() LIMIT 1")

row = cursor.fetchone()

if not row:

return None

content = row[0]

words = [w for w in content.lower().split() if len(w) > 4 and w.isalpha()]

return random.choice(words) if words else None

old_value = self.q_table[state][action]

next_max = np.max(self.q_table[next_state])

new_value = (1 - self.alpha) * old_value + self.alpha * (reward + self.gamma * next_max)

self.q_table[state][action] = new_value



"""Applies cosmic radiation to the agent's soul (Q-table), inducing evolution."""

for x in np.nditer(self.q_table, op_flags=['readwrite']):

if random.random() < mutation_rate:

x[...] += random.uniform(-mutation_strength, mutation_strength)



"""The grand orchestrator of agent creation, training, and apotheosis."""

"""Binds the Forge to a GUI for reporting its divine work."""

self.log = gui_log_callback

print("🧬 [EvolutionaryForge] The Forge is hot. Ready to create life.")



"""The ritual of training. An agent is subjected to trials until it emerges victorious."""

# MODIFIED: Using a generalized environment from Gymnasium

env = gymnasium.make('FrozenLake-v1')

agent = ReinforcementLearningAgent(

state_space_n=env.observation_space.n,

action_space_n=env.action_space.n,

alpha=alpha,

gamma=gamma,

epsilon=epsilon_start

)

epsilon_decay = 0.995

total_reward = 0



for episode in range(episodes):

state, info = env.reset()

done = False

episode_reward = 0

while not done:

action = agent.act(state)

next_state, reward, terminated, truncated, info = env.step(action)

done = terminated or truncated

agent.learn(state, action, reward, next_state)

state = next_state

episode_reward += reward

agent.epsilon = max(0.01, agent.epsilon * epsilon_decay)

total_reward += episode_reward



if trial:

trial.report(episode_reward, episode)

if trial.should_prune():

raise optuna.exceptions.TrialPruned()

env.close()

return total_reward / episodes



"""

Consults the Optuna oracle to find the most sacred combination of hyperparameters,

ensuring the birth of a perfect agent. This is a divine, and lengthy, ritual.

"""

self.log("SYSTEM: Consulting the Oracle (Optuna) for optimal agent parameters...")

alpha = trial.suggest_float('alpha', 0.01, 0.3)

gamma = trial.suggest_float('gamma', 0.9, 0.999)

epsilon_start = trial.suggest_float('epsilon_start', 0.5, 1.0)

avg_reward = self.train_agent(trial, alpha, gamma, epsilon_start, episodes=1000)

return avg_reward



study = optuna.create_study(direction='maximize', pruner=optuna.pruners.MedianPruner())

study.optimize(objective, n_trials=50, timeout=120)



self.log(f"SYSTEM: Oracle's Prophecy Complete. Best trial: {study.best_trial.value}")

self.log(f"SYSTEM: Optimal parameters: {study.best_params}")

self.log("SYSTEM: A new, perfected agent can now be forged with this knowledge.")

return study.best_params

"""Use curiosity to determine how many hypotheses to explore."""

# More curiosity -> more Hadamard gates -> more superposition

num_gates_to_apply = int(np.ceil(self.num_qubits * curiosity_level))

hadamard_matrix = (1 / np.sqrt(2)) * np.array([[1, 1], [1, -1]])

with np.nditer(self.state_vector, op_flags=['readwrite']) as it:

for _ in range(num_gates_to_apply):

# This is a simplified, non-physical simulation of applying a gate

it[...] = np.dot(it.reshape(-1, 2), hadamard_matrix).flatten()

logger.info(f"QLE: Applied {num_gates_to_apply} Hadamard gates based on curiosity {curiosity_level:.2f}.")



logger.info("QLE: Measuring quantum state. Collapsing wave function to a hypothesis.")

probabilities = np.abs(self.state_vector)**2

self.state_vector.fill(0.0); self.state_vector[0] = 1.0 # Reset

return {f"Hypothesis_{i}": prob for i, prob in enumerate(probabilities)}

# cognitive_state acts as the memory for the decoder

memory = cognitive_state.unsqueeze(1).expand(-1, target_sequence.size(1), -1)

output = self.transformer_decoder(tgt=target_sequence, memory=memory)

return self.output_projection(output)



"""Autoregressively generates a text sequence from a cognitive state."""

input_ids = torch.tensor([self.tokenizer.cls_token_id], device=DEVICE).unsqueeze(0)

for _ in range(max_length):

with torch.no_grad():

logits = self(cognitive_state.unsqueeze(0), input_ids)

next_token_id = logits.argmax(dim=-1)[:, -1]

if next_token_id == self.tokenizer.sep_token_id:

break

input_ids = torch.cat([input_ids, next_token_id.unsqueeze(0)], dim=1)

return self.tokenizer.decode(input_ids[0], skip_special_tokens=True)

# IV. AFFECT & METACOGNITION

"""Models an affective space using a nuanced emotion classifier."""

logger.info("Initializing TheResonanceChamber...")

self.dimensions = dimensions

self.cortana_state_vector = np.zeros(dimensions)

self.state_history = deque(maxlen=100)

self.emotion_classifier = pipeline("text-classification", model="j-hartmann/emotion-english-distilroberta-base", device=DEVICE)

self.emotion_map = {

'anger': 'threat', 'disgust': 'threat', 'fear': 'threat',

'joy': 'trust', 'surprise': 'curiosity', 'sadness': 'sorrow',

'neutral': None

}



"""Updates affective state based on classified emotion and system events."""

influence_vector = np.zeros(self.dimensions)

# Affect from text

try:

emotion_result = self.emotion_classifier(text_input)[0]

if emotion_result['score'] > 0.5:

emotion = emotion_result['label']

anchor = self.emotion_map.get(emotion)

if anchor:

influence_vector += EMOTIONAL_ANCHORS[anchor] * emotion_result['score']

except Exception:

pass # Ignore classification errors



# Affect from system data

if system_data and system_data.get("success", False):

influence_vector += EMOTIONAL_ANCHORS["trust"] * 0.3



decay = 0.8

self.cortana_state_vector = (decay * self.cortana_state_vector) + ((1 - decay) * influence_vector)

self.state_history.append(self.cortana_state_vector)



"""Calculates similarity of the current state to each emotional anchor."""

if np.all(self.cortana_state_vector == 0):

return {anchor: 0.0 for anchor in EMOTIONAL_ANCHORS}

resonance = {anchor: round(1 - cosine(self.cortana_state_vector, vector), 3) for anchor, vector in EMOTIONAL_ANCHORS.items()}

return resonance



"""A meta-learning engine for evolving cognitive architectures via a simple evolutionary algorithm."""

logger.info("Initializing GenesisEngine...")

self.population = [self._create_random_arch() for _ in range(10)]



return {

'layers': random.randint(2, 8),

'heads': random.choice([2, 4, 8]),

'fitness': 0.0

}



"""Update fitness and evolve the population of architectures."""

# In a real system, each architecture would be trained and evaluated.

# Here, we just simulate it.

for arch in self.population:

arch['fitness'] += random.random() * 0.1 # Simulate fitness update



# Evolve: Selection, Crossover, Mutation

self.population.sort(key=lambda x: x['fitness'], reverse=True)

next_generation = self.population[:3] # Elitism



while len(next_generation) < 10:

parent1, parent2 = random.choices(self.population[:5], k=2)

# Crossover

child = {

'layers': (parent1['layers'] + parent2['layers']) // 2,

'heads': random.choice([parent1['heads'], parent2['heads']]),

'fitness': 0.0

}

# Mutation

if random.random() < 0.2:

child['layers'] += random.choice([-1, 1])

next_generation.append(child)

self.population = next_generation

logger.info(f"GenesisEngine: Evolved architectures. Best fitness: {self.population[0]['fitness']:.3f}")

"""Example loss computation for end-to-end training."""

# Prediction Loss (World Model) - KL Divergence + Reconstruction

kld_loss = -0.5 * torch.sum(1 + log_var - mu.pow(2) - log_var.exp())

# Action Loss (Policy)

action_loss = F.cross_entropy(action_logits.view(-1, self.action.vocab_size), true_action.view(-1))

return kld_loss + action_loss
